# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Scheduler Framework Plugin Extension Points

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that define the scheduler framework plugin extension points: the PreFilter, Filter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, and PostBind interfaces and their registration in the scheduler framework.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

51-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer.json file that documents all the scheduler framework plugin extension points in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository.

## Summary

I found all 9 main scheduler framework plugin extension point interfaces defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/kube-scheduler/framework/interface.go`:

1. **PreFilterPlugin** - Called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle
2. **FilterPlugin** - Filters out nodes that cannot run a pod
3. **PostFilterPlugin** - Called after a pod cannot be scheduled
4. **PreScorePlugin** - Informational extension point with list of filtered nodes
5. **ScorePlugin** - Ranks nodes that passed filtering
6. **ReservePlugin** - Updates plugin state when scheduler cache is updated
7. **PreBindPlugin** - Called before a pod is bound (with new PreBindPreFlight method)
8. **BindPlugin** - Binds a pod to a node
9. **PostBindPlugin** - Called after a pod is successfully bound

The framework implementation in `pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go` contains the `frameworkImpl` struct with slices and Run* methods for each extension point. The plugin registry mechanism in `pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go` manages plugin registration.

The answer.json file at `/workspace/answer.json` contains the complete file listings, symbol definitions, initialization chain, and a detailed narrative explanation of all the extension points.

All PreFilter\\n479: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n480: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n510: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n511: \\t//\\n512: \\t// \\\"Error\\\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\\n513: \\t//\\n514: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n515: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n516: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n517: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n518: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n519: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n520: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n521: \\t//\\n522: \\t// Plugins are encouraged to check the context for cancellation.\\n523: \\t// Once canceled, they should return as soon as possible with\\n524: \\t// an UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status that includes the\\n525: \\t// `context.Cause(ctx)` error explanation. All PreFilter\n479: \t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n480: \t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n481: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n482: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n483: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n484: \t//\n485: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n486: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n487: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodes []NodeInfo) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n488: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n489: \t// or nil if it does not. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n491: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n492: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n493: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n494: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n495: }\n496: \n497: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n498: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n499: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n500: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n501: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n502: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n503: // running the pod. Plugins that implement FilterPlugin should\n504: // also implement SignPlugin to enable batching optimizations.\n505: type FilterPlugin interface {\n506: \tPlugin\n507: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n508: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n509: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n510: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n511: \t//\n512: \t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n513: \t//\n514: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n515: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n516: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n517: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n518: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n519: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n520: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n521: \t//\n522: \t// Plugins are encouraged to check the context for cancellation.\n523: \t// Once canceled, they should return as soon as possible with\n524: \t// an UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status that includes the\n525: \t// `context.Cause(ctx)` error explanation. For example, the\n526: \t// context gets canceled when a sufficient number of suitable\n527: \t// nodes have been found and searching for more isn't necessary\n528: \t// anymore.\n529: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo NodeInfo) *Status\n530: }\n531: \n532: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n533: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n534: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n535: \tPlugin\n536: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n537: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n538: \t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n539: \t//\n540: \t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n541: \t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n542: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n543: \t//\n544: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n545: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n546: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n547: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n548: \t//\n549: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n550: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n559: // state or to generate logs/metrics. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n575: \t// a success status.\n576: \tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n577: }\n578: \n579: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n580: // nodes that passed the filtering phase. This file contains the primary interface definitions for all scheduler plugin extension points.\\n\\nThe nine extension point interfaces are:\\n\\n1. **PreFilterPlugin** (lines 473-495): Called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. Plugins implementing PreFilterPlugin can return a PreFilterResult to filter out nodes early in the scheduling process.\\n\\n2. **FilterPlugin** (lines 505-530): Called at the filter extension point to exclude nodes that cannot run a pod. This concept was previously called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\\n\\n3. **PostFilterPlugin** (lines 532-554): Called after a pod cannot be scheduled. These plugins implement preemption logic or other recovery mechanisms.\\n\\n4. **PreScorePlugin** (lines 561-569): An informational extension point. Plugins are called with a list of nodes that passed the filtering phase.\\n\\n5. **ScorePlugin** (lines 582-591): Ranks nodes that passed the filtering phase. Each plugin returns a score for each node.\\n\\n6. **ReservePlugin** (lines 599-611): Plugins with Reserve and Unreserve methods that update plugin state when the scheduler cache is updated. Previously called 'assume' in the original scheduler.\\n\\n7. **PreBindPlugin** (lines 615-628): Called before a pod is bound. All prebind plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. Includes new PreBindPreFlight method for lightweight pre-checks.\\n\\n8. **BindPlugin** (lines 656-665): Used to bind a pod to a node. Only one bind plugin should handle a pod; others return Skip status.\\n\\n9. **PostBindPlugin** (lines 632-639): Called after a pod is successfully bound to a node. These plugins are informational and typically used for cleanup.\\n\\n10. **PermitPlugin** (lines 641-652): Called before binding a pod. Can prevent or delay binding with timeout duration.\\n\\nThe framework implementation in `pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go` contains the `frameworkImpl` struct (lines 57-100) which maintains slices for each plugin type:\\n- preFilterPlugins\\n- filterPlugins\\n- postFilterPlugins\\n- preScorePlugins\\n- scorePlugins\\n- reservePlugins\\n- preBindPlugins\\n- bindPlugins\\n- postBindPlugins\\n- permitPlugins\\n\\nThe framework also defines Run* methods that execute each extension point (e.g., RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins, etc.).\\n\\nThe plugin registry mechanism is implemented in `pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go` (lines 68-101). The Registry is a map of plugin names to PluginFactory functions. The Register method (lines 73-81) adds new plugins to the registry, and the Merge method (lines 93-101) merges multiple registries together.\\n\\nThe `pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go` file provides the Framework interface definition that declares the public methods for running each extension point's plugins, while `pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go` provides the CycleState interface for managing state between plugins during a scheduling cycle.\\n\\nThis architecture allows the scheduler to be extensible with custom plugins that implement the specific extension point interfaces, enabling users to customize the scheduling behavior for their specific cluster requirements.\"\n}\n",
